# Task: Understand ClickHouse MergeTree Storage Engine Architecture

## Objective
Produce a comprehensive architecture analysis of the MergeTree storage engine, the core table engine in ClickHouse, covering its data organization, merge process, and query execution path.

## Steps
1. Find the MergeTree implementation in `src/Storages/MergeTree/`
2. Trace the write path: how INSERTs create new data parts
3. Trace the merge path: how background merges combine parts
4. Trace the read path: how SELECT queries scan parts with index skipping
5. Create `architecture_analysis.md` in `/workspace/` documenting:
   - High-level MergeTree architecture diagram (text-based)
   - Data part structure (columns, marks, primary index, skip indices)
   - Write path: from INSERT to committed part
   - Merge path: merge selection, merge algorithm, part replacement
   - Read path: part pruning, mark selection, column reading
   - Key source files with their roles
   - At least 10 specific file paths referenced

## Key Reference Files
- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h` — base class
- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp` — write path
- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp` — merge logic
- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp` — read path

## Success Criteria
- architecture_analysis.md exists
- Covers write, merge, and read paths
- References at least 10 specific source files
- Describes data part structure

The architecture analysis has been written to `/workspace/architecture_analysis.md`. Here's a summary of what's covered:

## Document Summary

**`/workspace/architecture_analysis.md`** contains:

### Architecture Diagram
A text-based diagram showing the three main paths (write, merge, read) and how they interact through the shared Active Parts Set.

### Data Part Structure
- Part naming convention: `{partition_id}_{min_block}_{max_block}_{level}`
- Complete file listing inside a part directory (`.bin`, `.mrk2`, `primary.idx`, skip index files, `checksums.txt`, `partition.dat`, `minmax_*.idx`)
- Key fields of `IMergeTreeDataPart` (partition info, row count, granularity, MinMax index)
- Part lifecycle state machine: `Temporary → PreActive → Active → Outdated → Deleting`
- Constant vs. adaptive index granularity

### Write Path
Traces the full INSERT flow: `MergeTreeSink::consume()` → `splitBlockIntoParts()` → `writeTempPartImpl()` (partition computation, sorting, pre-merge for special engines, disk reservation, `MergedBlockOutputStream`) → atomic rename → commit to Active set.

### Merge Path
Covers merge selection (`SimpleMergeSelector`, `TTLMergeSelector`, `AllMergeSelector`), dynamic size limits based on pool occupancy, and `MergeTask`'s three-stage coroutine execution (horizontal merge, vertical merge for large parts, projection merge).

### Read Path
Covers three levels of filtering: partition pruning (MinMax + PartitionPruner), primary key index scan (`markRangesFromPKRange()` binary search), skip index filtering (bloom/minmax/set), and final data reading via `MergeTreeRangeReader` with PREWHERE optimization.

### References
**20+ specific source files** are cited throughout, well exceeding the 10-file minimum requirement.

  "content": "# ClickHouse MergeTree Storage Engine: Architecture Analysis\n\n## Overview\n\nMergeTree is ClickHouse's primary table engine family, designed for high-throughput ingestion and efficient analytical queries. The core idea is **incremental sorted storage**: INSERTs produce small sorted parts, which background merges combine into larger sorted parts. Queries skip irrelevant data using multi-level indexing.\n\n---\n\n## High-Level Architecture Diagram\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502     (background)         (query path) Data Part Structure\n\nA **data part** is the fundamental storage unit. Each part is an immutable directory containing sorted data for one partition range. Parts are named with the pattern `{partition_id}_{min_block}_{max_block}_{level}`.\n\n### Part Types\n\n| Type    | Description                                    | Source File |\n|---------|------------------------------------------------|-------------|\n| Wide    | One `.bin`/`.mrk` file per column              | `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWide.h` |\n| Compact | All columns packed into a single data file     | `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartCompact.h` |\n\n### Files Inside a Part Directory\n\n```\n{partition_id}_{min_block}_{max_block}_{level}/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 primary.idx            \u2014 Primary key index (every N-th row value)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 [column].bin           \u2014 Compressed column data (LZ4/ZSTD)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 [column].mrk2          \u2014 Mark file: offsets into .bin for each granule\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 skp_idx_[name].idx     \u2014 Skip index data (bloom filter, minmax, set, etc.)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 skp_idx_[name].mrk2    \u2014 Skip index marks\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 checksums.txt          \u2014 SHA256 checksums for all files\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 columns.txt            \u2014 Column names and types list\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 count.txt              \u2014 Total row count\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 partition.dat          \u2014 Serialized partition key value\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 minmax_[col].idx       \u2014 MinMax index for partition key columns\n```\n\n### Key Data Structures\n\n**`IMergeTreeDataPart`** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h`)\n- `info`: `MergeTreePartInfo` \u2014 partition id, min/max block numbers, level, mutation version\n- `rows_count`: total number of rows\n- `index_granularity`: marks structure (`MergeTreeIndexGranularity`)\n- `MinMaxIndex`: hyperrectangle of min/max values for partition columns (for part pruning)\n- `checksums`: `MergeTreeDataPartChecksums` \u2014 integrity verification\n- `columns`: `NamesAndTypesList` \u2014 schema at time of write\n\n**Part lifecycle states** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartState.h`):\n```\nTemporary \u2192 PreActive \u2192 Active \u2192 Outdated \u2192 Deleting \u2192 (deleted)\n```\n\n### Index Granularity\n\n`MergeTreeIndexGranularity` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularity.h`) defines the granule structure \u2014 groups of rows (typically 8192 rows or ~10MB uncompressed) that are the smallest unit of I/O. Each granule has a corresponding mark entry.\n\n- **Constant granularity**: all granules have the same row count (older format, `.mrk` files)\n- **Adaptive granularity**: granules sized by bytes (newer format, `.mrk2` files)\n\n---\n\n## Write Path: INSERT to Committed Part\n\n### Entry Point: `MergeTreeSink`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp`\n\nThe sink is the pipeline processor that receives `Chunk` objects from the query executor.\n\n```\nINSERT query\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\nMergeTreeSink::consume(chunk)\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 1. MergeTreeDataWriter::splitBlockIntoParts()\n    \u2502       Split the incoming block by partition key values.\n    \u2502       Each sub-block belongs to one partition.\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 2. For each partition block:\n    \u2502       MergeTreeDataWriter::writeTempPart()\n    \u2502           \u2192 writeTempPartImpl()\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 3. finishDelayedChunk()\n            Commit each temp part to the active set\n```\n\n### `MergeTreeDataWriter::writeTempPartImpl`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp`\n\nKey steps inside `writeTempPartImpl`:\n\n1. **Partition & MinMax computation**: Compute the partition ID and update the MinMax index for partition columns.\n\n2. **Expression evaluation**: Execute the sorting key and skip index expressions on the block to produce derived columns.\n\n3. **Sorting**: If the block is not already sorted by the primary key, compute a stable permutation (`stableGetPermutation`). Optional `optimize_row_order` (Hilbert curve reordering) for better compression.\n\n4. **Pre-merge (optimize_on_insert)**: For non-Ordinary engines (ReplacingMergeTree, SummingMergeTree, etc.), `mergeBlock()` runs the engine-specific algorithm within the single block (deduplication, collapsing, summing).\n\n5. **Disk reservation**: Reserve space on the appropriate disk volume, respecting TTL volume rules.\n\n6. **Writing via `MergedBlockOutputStream`**: Write sorted data to a temp directory (`tmp_insert_<partname>/`), producing all `.bin`, `.mrk2`, `primary.idx`, and skip index files.\n\n7. **Finalization**: `TemporaryPart::finalize()` \u2192 calls `precommitTransaction()` on the storage layer, and optionally warms mark/index caches.\n\n### `MergedBlockOutputStream`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.h`\n\nWrites one part worth of data. Internally uses:\n- `MergeTreeDataPartWriterWide` or `MergeTreeDataPartWriterCompact`\n- Writes columns as compressed blocks (`.bin`)\n- Writes granule offsets as marks (`.mrk2`)\n- Writes the sparse primary index (`primary.idx`) \u2014 one entry per granule\n- Writes skip index data and marks\n\n### Part Commit\n\nAfter `writeTempPart` returns a `TemporaryPart`:\n- The temp directory is **renamed** to its final part name (atomic filesystem rename)\n- The part is inserted into `MergeTreeData`'s `data_parts_by_info` set as `PreActive` then `Active`\n- `PartLog` is written for observability\n\n---\n\n## Merge Path: Background Merge Process\n\n### Merge Selection\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp`\n\nThe background executor (`MergeTreeBackgroundExecutor`) periodically calls:\n\n```\nMergeTreeDataMergerMutator::selectPartsToMerge()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 getDataPartsToSelectMergeFrom()\n    \u2502       Get all Active parts (or Active+some Outdated if MVCC transactions active)\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 getPossibleMergeRanges()\n    \u2502       Group parts by partition. Within each partition, identify\n    \u2502       contiguous ranges of mergeable parts (same partition, no gaps in block range).\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 selectPartsToMergeFromRanges()\n            Apply merge selector algorithm to pick the best range to merge.\n```\n\n**Merge selectors** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/`):\n- `SimpleMergeSelector` \u2014 default; uses a scoring function balancing part count, size, and age. Controlled by `merge_selector_base`, `merge_selector_window_size`, etc.\n- `AllMergeSelector` \u2014 merges all parts in a partition (used by `OPTIMIZE TABLE FINAL`)\n- `TTLMergeSelector` \u2014 prioritizes parts where TTL expiry is imminent\n\n**Size limits**: `getMaxSourcePartsSizeForMerge()` dynamically limits merge size based on pool occupancy \u2014 more free threads \u2192 allow larger merges.\n\n### Merge Execution: `MergeTask`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.h`, `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp`\n\n`MergeTask` is a coroutine-style task that executes merge in stages, yielding between blocks:\n\n```\nMergeTask::execute()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 1: Horizontal merge\n    \u2502       Open MergeTreeSequentialSource for each source part\n    \u2502       Feed into engine-specific sorted merge transform:\n    \u2502         - MergingSortedTransform      (Ordinary)\n    \u2502         - ReplacingSortedTransform    (ReplacingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - CollapsingSortedTransform   (CollapsingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - SummingSortedTransform      (SummingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - AggregatingSortedTransform  (AggregatingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - VersionedCollapsingTransform\n    \u2502         - GraphiteRollupSortedTransform\n    \u2502       Write output via MergedBlockOutputStream\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 2: Vertical merge (if enabled, for wide parts)\n    \u2502       Re-read each non-key column independently and write them\n    \u2502       using MergedColumnOnlyOutputStream \u2014 avoids loading all\n    \u2502       columns into memory simultaneously for large merges.\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 Stage 3: Projection merge\n            Re-merge projection parts to match the new merged part\n```\n\n### Part Replacement\n\nAfter the merged part is written:\n1. The new part is **renamed** from temp to its final name\n2. `MergeTreeData::renameMergedTemporaryPart()` atomically:\n   - Adds the new merged part as `Active`\n   - Marks the source parts as `Outdated`\n3. Source parts are later garbage-collected by the cleanup thread once no active queries reference them\n\n---\n\n## Read Path: SELECT Query Execution\n\n### Entry Point: `MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp`\n\n```\nSELECT query\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\nMergeTreeDataSelectExecutor::read()\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\nreadFromParts()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 1. filterPartsByVirtualColumns()    \u2014 filter by _part, _partition_id virtual columns\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 2. filterPartsByPartition()         \u2014 partition pruning\n    \u2502       a. MinMax index check on partition key columns\n    \u2502       b. PartitionPruner: evaluate partition key expression against WHERE\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 3. markRangesFromPKRange()          \u2014 primary index scan\n    \u2502       Binary search on primary.idx to find mark ranges\n    \u2502       that may contain rows matching the WHERE condition\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 4. Skip index filtering             \u2014 skip index evaluation\n    \u2502       For each skip index (bloom, minmax, set, etc.):\n    \u2502       Read skip index granules and eliminate mark ranges\n    \u2502       that are provably irrelevant\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 5. Build read plan\n            Create MergeTreeReadPool distributing mark ranges to threads\n            Each thread: MergeTreeSelectProcessor \u2192 MergeTreeRangeReader\n```\n\n### Partition Pruning\n\n`filterPartsByPartition()` applies two levels of coarse filtering before touching the primary index:\n\n1. **MinMax index** (`minmax_[col].idx`): Each part stores min/max values for each column in the partition expression. If the WHERE clause cannot overlap the part's min/max hyperrectangle, the part is skipped entirely.\n\n2. **PartitionPruner** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.h`): Evaluates the partition key expression against WHERE conditions using `KeyCondition` logic.\n\n### Primary Key Index Scan\n\n**`markRangesFromPKRange()`** in `MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp`:\n\nThe `primary.idx` file stores the primary key values for every N-th row (first row of each granule). A binary search on this in-memory index identifies which mark ranges **may** contain matching rows.\n\n`KeyCondition` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.h`) translates the WHERE clause into range conditions on the primary key, using monotonicity analysis to handle arbitrary expressions.\n\n### Skip Index Filtering\n\nAfter primary key scan narrows to a set of mark ranges, skip indices further eliminate granules:\n\n- **MinMax skip index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexMinMax.h`): stores min/max per granule\n- **Bloom filter skip index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexBloomFilter.h`): probabilistic membership test\n- **Set skip index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexSet.h`): stores small set of distinct values per granule\n- **Full-text index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexFullText.h`): inverted index for text search\n\n`MergeTreeIndexReader` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexReader.h`) reads skip index data for the selected mark ranges.\n\n### Data Reading\n\n`MergeTreeRangeReader` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp`):\n- Reads granules in the selected mark ranges from `.bin` files using offsets from `.mrk2`\n- Supports **PREWHERE** optimization: reads a cheap filter column first, evaluates the filter, then reads remaining columns only for matching rows\n- Uses `IMergeTreeReader` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeReader.h`) \u2014 either `MergeTreeReaderWide` or `MergeTreeReaderCompact`\n\n`MergeTreeReadPool` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.h`) distributes mark ranges across parallel reader threads for multi-threaded scanning.\n\n---\n\n## Key Source Files Reference\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h` | Base class for all MergeTree variants; manages the active parts set, metadata, and shared state |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h` | Abstract The core idea is **incremental sorted storage**: INSERTs produce small sorted parts, which background merges combine into larger sorted parts. Queries skip irrelevant data using multi-level indexing.\n\n---\n\n## High-Level Architecture Data Part Structure\n\nA **data part** is the fundamental storage unit. Each part is an immutable directory containing sorted data for one partition range. Parts are named with the pattern `{partition_id}_{min_block}_{max_block}_{level}`.\n\n### Part Types\n\n| Type    | Description                                    | Source File |\n|---------|------------------------------------------------|-------------|\n| Wide    | One `.bin`/`.mrk` file per column              | `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWide.h` |\n| Compact | All columns packed into a single data file     | `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartCompact.h` |\n\n### Files Inside a Part Directory\n\n```\n{partition_id}_{min_block}_{max_block}_{level}/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 primary.idx            \u2014 Primary key index (every N-th row value)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 [column].bin           \u2014 Compressed column data (LZ4/ZSTD)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 [column].mrk2          \u2014 Mark file: offsets into .bin for each granule\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 skp_idx_[name].idx     \u2014 Skip index data (bloom filter, minmax, set, etc.)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 skp_idx_[name].mrk2    \u2014 Skip index marks\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 checksums.txt          \u2014 SHA256 checksums for all files\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 columns.txt            \u2014 Column names and types list\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 count.txt              \u2014 Total row count\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 partition.dat          \u2014 Serialized partition key value\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 minmax_[col].idx       \u2014 MinMax index for partition key columns\n```\n\n### Key Data Structures\n\n**`IMergeTreeDataPart`** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h`)\n- `info`: `MergeTreePartInfo` \u2014 partition id, min/max block numbers, level, mutation version\n- `rows_count`: total number of rows\n- `index_granularity`: marks structure (`MergeTreeIndexGranularity`)\n- `MinMaxIndex`: hyperrectangle of min/max values for partition columns (for part pruning)\n- `checksums`: `MergeTreeDataPartChecksums` \u2014 integrity verification\n- `columns`: `NamesAndTypesList` \u2014 schema at time of write\n\n**Part lifecycle states** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartState.h`):\n```\nTemporary \u2192 PreActive \u2192 Active \u2192 Outdated \u2192 Deleting \u2192 (deleted)\n```\n\n### Index Granularity\n\n`MergeTreeIndexGranularity` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularity.h`) defines the granule structure \u2014 groups of rows (typically 8192 rows or ~10MB uncompressed) that are the smallest unit of I/O. Each granule has a corresponding mark entry.\n\n- **Constant granularity**: all granules have the same row count (older format, `.mrk` files)\n- **Adaptive granularity**: granules sized by bytes (newer format, `.mrk2` files)\n\n---\n\n## Write Path: INSERT to Committed Part\n\n### Entry Point: `MergeTreeSink`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp`\n\nThe sink is the pipeline processor that receives `Chunk` objects from the query executor.\n\n```\nINSERT query\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\nMergeTreeSink::consume(chunk)\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 1. MergeTreeDataWriter::splitBlockIntoParts()\n    \u2502       Split the incoming block by partition key values.\n    \u2502       Each sub-block belongs to one partition.\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 2. For each partition block:\n    \u2502       MergeTreeDataWriter::writeTempPart()\n    \u2502           \u2192 writeTempPartImpl()\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 3. finishDelayedChunk()\n            Commit each temp part to the active set\n```\n\n### `MergeTreeDataWriter::writeTempPartImpl`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp`\n\nKey steps inside `writeTempPartImpl`:\n\n1. **Partition & MinMax computation**: Compute the partition ID and update the MinMax index for partition columns.\n\n2. **Expression evaluation**: Execute the sorting key and skip index expressions on the block to produce derived columns.\n\n3. **Sorting**: If the block is not already sorted by the primary key, compute a stable permutation (`stableGetPermutation`). Optional `optimize_row_order` (Hilbert curve reordering) for better compression.\n\n4. **Pre-merge (optimize_on_insert)**: For non-Ordinary engines (ReplacingMergeTree, SummingMergeTree, etc.), `mergeBlock()` runs the engine-specific algorithm within the single block (deduplication, collapsing, summing).\n\n5. **Disk reservation**: Reserve space on the appropriate disk volume, respecting TTL volume rules.\n\n6. **Writing via `MergedBlockOutputStream`**: Write sorted data to a temp directory (`tmp_insert_<partname>/`), producing all `.bin`, `.mrk2`, `primary.idx`, and skip index files.\n\n7. **Finalization**: `TemporaryPart::finalize()` calls `precommitTransaction()` on the storage layer, and optionally warms mark/index caches.\n\n### `MergedBlockOutputStream`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.h`\n\nWrites one part worth of data. Internally uses:\n- `MergeTreeDataPartWriterWide` or `MergeTreeDataPartWriterCompact`\n- Writes columns as compressed blocks (`.bin`)\n- Writes granule offsets as marks (`.mrk2`)\n- Writes the sparse primary index (`primary.idx`) \u2014 one entry per granule\n- Writes skip index data and marks\n\n### Part Commit\n\nAfter `writeTempPart` returns a `TemporaryPart`:\n- The temp directory is **renamed** to its final part name (atomic filesystem rename)\n- The part is inserted into `MergeTreeData`'s `data_parts_by_info` set as `PreActive` then `Active`\n- `PartLog` is written for observability\n\n---\n\n## Merge Path: Background Merge Process\n\n### Merge Selection\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp`\n\nThe background executor (`MergeTreeBackgroundExecutor`) periodically calls:\n\n```\nMergeTreeDataMergerMutator::selectPartsToMerge()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 getDataPartsToSelectMergeFrom()\n    \u2502       Get all Active parts (or Active+some Outdated if MVCC transactions active)\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 getPossibleMergeRanges()\n    \u2502       Group parts by partition. Within each partition, identify\n    \u2502       contiguous ranges of mergeable parts (same partition, no gaps in block range).\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 selectPartsToMergeFromRanges()\n            Apply merge selector algorithm to pick the best range to merge.\n```\n\n**Merge selectors** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/`):\n- `SimpleMergeSelector` \u2014 default; uses a scoring function balancing part count, size, and age. Controlled by `merge_selector_base`, `merge_selector_window_size`, etc.\n- `AllMergeSelector` \u2014 merges all parts in a partition (used by `OPTIMIZE TABLE FINAL`)\n- `TTLMergeSelector` \u2014 prioritizes parts where TTL expiry is imminent\n\n**Size limits**: `getMaxSourcePartsSizeForMerge()` dynamically limits merge size based on pool occupancy \u2014 more free threads allow larger merges.\n\n### Merge Execution: `MergeTask`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.h`, `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp`\n\n`MergeTask` is a coroutine-style task that executes merge in stages, yielding between blocks to allow priority-based scheduling (smaller merges get higher priority):\n\n```\nMergeTask::execute()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 1: Horizontal merge\n    \u2502       Open MergeTreeSequentialSource for each source part\n    \u2502       Feed into engine-specific sorted merge transform:\n    \u2502         - MergingSortedTransform      (Ordinary)\n    \u2502         - ReplacingSortedTransform    (ReplacingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - CollapsingSortedTransform   (CollapsingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - SummingSortedTransform      (SummingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - AggregatingSortedTransform  (AggregatingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - VersionedCollapsingTransform\n    \u2502         - GraphiteRollupSortedTransform\n    \u2502       Write output via MergedBlockOutputStream\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 2: Vertical merge (if enabled, for wide parts)\n    \u2502       Re-read each non-key column independently and write them\n    \u2502       using MergedColumnOnlyOutputStream \u2014 avoids loading all\n    \u2502       columns into memory simultaneously for large merges.\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 Stage 3: Projection merge\n            Re-merge projection parts to match the new merged part\n```\n\n### Part Replacement\n\nAfter the merged part is written:\n1. The new part is **renamed** from temp to its final name\n2. `MergeTreeData::renameMergedTemporaryPart()` atomically:\n   - Adds the new merged part as `Active`\n   - Marks the source parts as `Outdated`\n3. Source parts are later garbage-collected by the cleanup thread once no active queries reference them\n\n---\n\n## Read Path: SELECT Query Execution\n\n### Entry Point: `MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp`\n\n```\nSELECT query\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\nMergeTreeDataSelectExecutor::read()\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\nreadFromParts()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 1. filterPartsByVirtualColumns()    \u2014 filter by _part, _partition_id virtual columns\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 2. filterPartsByPartition()         \u2014 partition pruning\n    \u2502       a. MinMax index check on partition key columns\n    \u2502       b. PartitionPruner: evaluate partition key expression against WHERE\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 3. markRangesFromPKRange()          \u2014 primary index scan\n    \u2502       Binary search on primary.idx to find mark ranges\n    \u2502       that may contain rows matching the WHERE condition\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 4. Skip index filtering             \u2014 skip index evaluation\n    \u2502       For each skip index (bloom, minmax, set, etc.):\n    \u2502       Read skip index granules and eliminate mark ranges\n    \u2502       that are provably irrelevant\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 5. Build read plan\n            Create MergeTreeReadPool distributing mark ranges to threads\n            Each thread: MergeTreeSelectProcessor \u2192 MergeTreeRangeReader\n```\n\n### Partition Pruning\n\n`filterPartsByPartition()` applies two levels of coarse filtering before touching the primary index:\n\n1. **MinMax index** (`minmax_[col].idx`): Each part stores min/max values for each column in the partition expression. If the WHERE clause cannot overlap the part's min/max hyperrectangle, the part is skipped entirely.\n\n2. **PartitionPruner** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.h`): Evaluates the partition key expression against WHERE conditions using `KeyCondition` logic.\n\n### Primary Key Index Scan\n\n**`markRangesFromPKRange()`** in `MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp`:\n\nThe `primary.idx` file stores the primary key values for every N-th row (first row of each granule). A binary search on this in-memory index identifies which mark ranges **may** contain matching rows.\n\n`KeyCondition` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.h`) translates the WHERE clause into range conditions on the primary key, using monotonicity analysis to handle arbitrary expressions.\n\n### Skip Index Filtering\n\nAfter the primary key scan narrows to a set of mark ranges, skip indices further eliminate granules:\n\n- **MinMax skip index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexMinMax.h`): stores min/max per granule\n- **Bloom filter skip index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexBloomFilter.h`): probabilistic membership test\n- **Set skip index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexSet.h`): stores small set of distinct values per granule\n- **Full-text index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexFullText.h`): inverted index for text search\n\n`MergeTreeIndexReader` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexReader.h`) reads skip index data for the selected mark ranges.\n\n### Data Reading\n\n`MergeTreeRangeReader` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp`):\n- Reads granules in the selected mark ranges from `.bin` files using offsets from `.mrk2`\n- Supports **PREWHERE** optimization: reads a cheap filter column first, evaluates the filter, then reads remaining columns only for matching rows\n- Uses `IMergeTreeReader` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeReader.h`) \u2014 either `MergeTreeReaderWide` or `MergeTreeReaderCompact`\n\n`MergeTreeReadPool` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.h`) distributes mark ranges across parallel reader threads for multi-threaded scanning.\n\n---\n\n## Key Source Files Reference\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h` | Base class for all MergeTree variants; manages the active parts set, metadata, and shared state |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h` | Abstract data part interface; defines part structure, metadata, and state transitions |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp` | Write path: splits blocks by partition, sorts, and writes temp parts |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp` | Pipeline sink for INSERT; coordinates writing and committing temp parts |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.h` | Low-level part writer: produces `.bin`, `.mrk2`, `primary.idx`, skip index files |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp` | Merge selection logic: chooses which parts to merge and executes merges |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.h` | Coroutine-based merge executor with horizontal, vertical, and projection stages |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp` | Merge task implementation |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp` | Read path: partition pruning, primary index scan, skip index filtering, read plan |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.h` | Translates WHERE expressions into primary key range conditions for index scan |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp` | Reads mark ranges from parts with PREWHERE support |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.h` | Distributes mark ranges across parallel reader threads |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularity.h` | Index granularity abstraction (constant vs. adaptive granule sizes) |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartState.h` | Part lifecycle state machine (Temporary \u2192 PreActive \u2192 Active \u2192 Outdated \u2192 Deleting) |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWide.h` | Wide format: one file per column (used for larger parts) |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartCompact.h` | Compact format: all columns in one file (used for small/fresh parts) |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.h` | Partition-level pruning using the partition key expression |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeBackgroundExecutor.h` | Thread pool executor for background merge/mutation tasks |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/SimpleMergeSelector.h` | Default merge selector: balances size, count, and age heuristics |\n\n---\n\n## MergeTree Engine Variants\n\nAll engine variants share the same storage architecture but differ in their merge behavior:\n\n| Engine | Merge behavior | Controlled by |\n|--------|---------------|---------------|\n| `MergeTree` | Ordinary: no deduplication, just sorting | \u2014 |\n| `ReplacingMergeTree` | Keep only the latest version per primary key | `version_column`, `is_deleted_column` |\n| `SummingMergeTree` | Sum numeric columns per primary key | `columns_to_sum` |\n| `AggregatingMergeTree` | Merge aggregate function states per key | aggregate function column types |\n| `CollapsingMergeTree` | Cancel pairs of rows via sign column | `sign_column` |\n| `VersionedCollapsingMergeTree` | Collapsing with explicit version | `sign_column`, `version_column` |\n| `GraphiteMergeTree` | Rollup time-series data | `graphite_rollup_params` |\n\nThe merge algorithm for each variant is implemented in `src/Processors/Merges/Algorithms/` and selected in `MergeTreeDataWriter::mergeBlock()` and `MergeTask`.\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Data Flow\n\n```\nINSERT\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\nsplitBlockIntoParts()  \u2014 one sub-block per partition key value\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\nwriteTempPartImpl()    \u2014 sort by primary key, write compressed columns + marks + primary.idx\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\nrename tmp_insert_xxx \u2192 committed part name\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\ndata_parts_by_info: Temporary \u2192 PreActive \u2192 Active\n\n                    \u2502                    \u2502\n                    \u2502  (background)       \u2502  (SELECT query)\n                    \u25bc                    \u25bc\n         selectPartsToMerge()    filterPartsByPartition()\n                    \u2502 Active  skip index filtering\n         source parts \u2192 Outdated   (bloom/minmax/set per granule)\n                                        \u2502\n                                        \u25bc\n   "content": "# ClickHouse MergeTree Storage Engine: Architecture Analysis\n\n## Overview\n\nMergeTree is ClickHouse's primary table engine family, designed for high-throughput ingestion and efficient analytical queries. The core idea is **incremental sorted storage**: INSERTs produce small sorted parts, which background merges combine into larger sorted parts. Queries skip irrelevant data using multi-level indexing.\n\n---\n\n## High-Level Architecture Diagram\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502                         MergeTree Table                             \u2502\n\u2502                                                                     \u2502\n\u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502   INSERT     \u2502  \u2502            Data Parts (on disk)          \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502   path       \u2502  \u2502                                          \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502              \u2502  \u2502  partition_id_min_max_level/             \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502 MergeTreeSink\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500\u2500 primary.idx   (primary key index)  \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502        \u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500\u2500 [col].bin     (column data)        \u2502    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502     \u25bc        \u2502 \u2502\n\u2502         \u25bc                         \u2502                   \u2502            \u2502\n\u2502 \u2502\n\u2502  commit to Active        MergeTreeData        MergeTreeData        \u2502\n\u2502                          MergerMutator        SelectExecutor        \u2502\n\u2502                          (background)         (query path) Data Part Structure\n\nA **data part** is the fundamental storage unit. Each part is an immutable directory containing sorted data for one partition range. Parts are named with the pattern `{partition_id}_{min_block}_{max_block}_{level}`.\n\n### Part Types\n\n| Type    | Description                                    | Source File |\n|---------|------------------------------------------------|-------------|\n| Wide    | One `.bin`/`.mrk` file per column              | `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWide.h` |\n| Compact | All columns packed into a single data file     | `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartCompact.h` |\n\n### Files Inside a Part Directory\n\n```\n{partition_id}_{min_block}_{max_block}_{level}/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 primary.idx            \u2014 Primary key index (every N-th row value)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 [column].bin           \u2014 Compressed column data (LZ4/ZSTD)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 [column].mrk2          \u2014 Mark file: offsets into .bin for each granule\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 skp_idx_[name].idx     \u2014 Skip index data (bloom filter, minmax, set, etc.)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 skp_idx_[name].mrk2    \u2014 Skip index marks\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 checksums.txt          \u2014 SHA256 checksums for all files\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 columns.txt            \u2014 Column names and types list\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 count.txt              \u2014 Total row count\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 partition.dat          \u2014 Serialized partition key value\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 minmax_[col].idx       \u2014 MinMax index for partition key columns\n```\n\n### Key Data Structures\n\n**`IMergeTreeDataPart`** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h`)\n- `info`: `MergeTreePartInfo` \u2014 partition id, min/max block numbers, level, mutation version\n- `rows_count`: total number of rows\n- `index_granularity`: marks structure (`MergeTreeIndexGranularity`)\n- `MinMaxIndex`: hyperrectangle of min/max values for partition columns (for part pruning)\n- `checksums`: `MergeTreeDataPartChecksums` \u2014 integrity verification\n- `columns`: `NamesAndTypesList` \u2014 schema at time of write\n\n**Part lifecycle states** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartState.h`):\n```\nTemporary \u2192 PreActive \u2192 Active \u2192 Outdated \u2192 Deleting \u2192 (deleted)\n```\n\n### Index Granularity\n\n`MergeTreeIndexGranularity` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularity.h`) defines the granule structure \u2014 groups of rows (typically 8192 rows or ~10MB uncompressed) that are the smallest unit of I/O. Each granule has a corresponding mark entry.\n\n- **Constant granularity**: all granules have the same row count (older format, `.mrk` files)\n- **Adaptive granularity**: granules sized by bytes (newer format, `.mrk2` files)\n\n---\n\n## Write Path: INSERT to Committed Part\n\n### Entry Point: `MergeTreeSink`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp`\n\nThe sink is the pipeline processor that receives `Chunk` objects from the query executor.\n\n```\nINSERT query\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\nMergeTreeSink::consume(chunk)\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 1. MergeTreeDataWriter::splitBlockIntoParts()\n    \u2502       Split the incoming block by partition key values.\n    \u2502       Each sub-block belongs to one partition.\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 2. For each partition block:\n    \u2502       MergeTreeDataWriter::writeTempPart()\n    \u2502           \u2192 writeTempPartImpl()\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 3. finishDelayedChunk()\n            Commit each temp part to the active set\n```\n\n### `MergeTreeDataWriter::writeTempPartImpl`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp`\n\nKey steps inside `writeTempPartImpl`:\n\n1. **Partition & MinMax computation**: Compute the partition ID and update the MinMax index for partition columns.\n\n2. **Expression evaluation**: Execute the sorting key and skip index expressions on the block to produce derived columns.\n\n3. **Sorting**: If the block is not already sorted by the primary key, compute a stable permutation (`stableGetPermutation`). Optional `optimize_row_order` (Hilbert curve reordering) for better compression.\n\n4. **Pre-merge (optimize_on_insert)**: For non-Ordinary engines (ReplacingMergeTree, SummingMergeTree, etc.), `mergeBlock()` runs the engine-specific algorithm within the single block (deduplication, collapsing, summing).\n\n5. **Disk reservation**: Reserve space on the appropriate disk volume, respecting TTL volume rules.\n\n6. **Writing via `MergedBlockOutputStream`**: Write sorted data to a temp directory (`tmp_insert_<partname>/`), producing all `.bin`, `.mrk2`, `primary.idx`, and skip index files.\n\n7. **Finalization**: `TemporaryPart::finalize()` calls `precommitTransaction()` on the storage layer, and optionally warms mark/index caches.\n\n### `MergedBlockOutputStream`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.h`\n\nWrites one part worth of data. Internally uses:\n- `MergeTreeDataPartWriterWide` or `MergeTreeDataPartWriterCompact`\n- Writes columns as compressed blocks (`.bin`)\n- Writes granule offsets as marks (`.mrk2`)\n- Writes the sparse primary index (`primary.idx`) \u2014 one entry per granule\n- Writes skip index data and marks\n\n### Part Commit\n\nAfter `writeTempPart` returns a `TemporaryPart`:\n- The temp directory is **renamed** to its final part name (atomic filesystem rename)\n- The part is inserted into `MergeTreeData`'s `data_parts_by_info` set as `PreActive` then `Active`\n- `PartLog` is written for observability\n\n---\n\n## Merge Path: Background Merge Process\n\n### Merge Selection\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp`\n\nThe background executor (`MergeTreeBackgroundExecutor`) periodically calls:\n\n```\nMergeTreeDataMergerMutator::selectPartsToMerge()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 getDataPartsToSelectMergeFrom()\n    \u2502       Get all Active parts (or Active+some Outdated if MVCC transactions active)\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 getPossibleMergeRanges()\n    \u2502       Group parts by partition. Within each partition, identify\n    \u2502       contiguous ranges of mergeable parts (same partition, no gaps in block range).\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 selectPartsToMergeFromRanges()\n            Apply merge selector algorithm to pick the best range to merge.\n```\n\n**Merge selectors** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/`):\n- `SimpleMergeSelector` \u2014 default; uses a scoring function balancing part count, size, and age. Controlled by `merge_selector_base`, `merge_selector_window_size`, etc.\n- `AllMergeSelector` \u2014 merges all parts in a partition (used by `OPTIMIZE TABLE FINAL`)\n- `TTLMergeSelector` \u2014 prioritizes parts where TTL expiry is imminent\n\n**Size limits**: `getMaxSourcePartsSizeForMerge()` dynamically limits merge size based on pool occupancy \u2014 more free threads allow larger merges.\n\n### Merge Execution: `MergeTask`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.h`, `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp`\n\n`MergeTask` is a coroutine-style task that executes merge in stages, yielding between blocks to allow priority-based scheduling (smaller merges get higher priority):\n\n```\nMergeTask::execute()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 1: Horizontal merge\n    \u2502       Open MergeTreeSequentialSource for each source part\n    \u2502       Feed into engine-specific sorted merge transform:\n    \u2502         - MergingSortedTransform      (Ordinary)\n    \u2502         - ReplacingSortedTransform    (ReplacingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - CollapsingSortedTransform   (CollapsingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - SummingSortedTransform      (SummingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - AggregatingSortedTransform  (AggregatingMergeTree)\n    \u2502         - VersionedCollapsingTransform\n    \u2502         - GraphiteRollupSortedTransform\n    \u2502       Write output via MergedBlockOutputStream\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 Stage 2: Vertical merge (if enabled, for wide parts)\n    \u2502       Re-read each non-key column independently and write them\n    \u2502       using MergedColumnOnlyOutputStream \u2014 avoids loading all\n    \u2502       columns into memory simultaneously for large merges.\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 Stage 3: Projection merge\n            Re-merge projection parts to match the new merged part\n```\n\n### Part Replacement\n\nAfter the merged part is written:\n1. The new part is **renamed** from temp to its final name\n2. `MergeTreeData::renameMergedTemporaryPart()` atomically:\n   - Adds the new merged part as `Active`\n   - Marks the source parts as `Outdated`\n3. Source parts are later garbage-collected by the cleanup thread once no active queries reference them\n\n---\n\n## Read Path: SELECT Query Execution\n\n### Entry Point: `MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor`\n**File:** `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp`\n\n```\nSELECT query\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\nMergeTreeDataSelectExecutor::read()\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\nreadFromParts()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 1. filterPartsByVirtualColumns()    \u2014 filter by _part, _partition_id virtual columns\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 2. filterPartsByPartition()         \u2014 partition pruning\n    \u2502       a. MinMax index check on partition key columns\n    \u2502       b. PartitionPruner: evaluate partition key expression against WHERE\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 3. markRangesFromPKRange()          \u2014 primary index scan\n    \u2502       Binary search on primary.idx to find mark ranges\n    \u2502       that may contain rows matching the WHERE condition\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500 4. Skip index filtering             \u2014 skip index evaluation\n    \u2502       For each skip index (bloom, minmax, set, etc.):\n    \u2502       Read skip index granules and eliminate mark ranges\n    \u2502       that are provably irrelevant\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500 5. Build read plan\n            Create MergeTreeReadPool distributing mark ranges to threads\n            Each thread: MergeTreeSelectProcessor \u2192 MergeTreeRangeReader\n```\n\n### Partition Pruning\n\n`filterPartsByPartition()` applies two levels of coarse filtering before touching the primary index:\n\n1. **MinMax index** (`minmax_[col].idx`): Each part stores min/max values for each column in the partition expression. If the WHERE clause cannot overlap the part's min/max hyperrectangle, the part is skipped entirely.\n\n2. **PartitionPruner** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.h`): Evaluates the partition key expression against WHERE conditions using `KeyCondition` logic.\n\n### Primary Key Index Scan\n\n**`markRangesFromPKRange()`** in `MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp`:\n\nThe `primary.idx` file stores the primary key values for every N-th row (first row of each granule). A binary search on this in-memory index identifies which mark ranges **may** contain matching rows.\n\n`KeyCondition` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.h`) translates the WHERE clause into range conditions on the primary key, using monotonicity analysis to handle arbitrary expressions.\n\n### Skip Index Filtering\n\nAfter the primary key scan narrows to a set of mark ranges, skip indices further eliminate granules:\n\n- **MinMax skip index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexMinMax.h`): stores min/max per granule\n- **Bloom filter skip index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexBloomFilter.h`): probabilistic membership test\n- **Set skip index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexSet.h`): stores small set of distinct values per granule\n- **Full-text index** (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexFullText.h`): inverted index for text search\n\n`MergeTreeIndexReader` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexReader.h`) reads skip index data for the selected mark ranges.\n\n### Data Reading\n\n`MergeTreeRangeReader` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp`):\n- Reads granules in the selected mark ranges from `.bin` files using offsets from `.mrk2`\n- Supports **PREWHERE** optimization: reads a cheap filter column first, evaluates the filter, then reads remaining columns only for matching rows\n- Uses `IMergeTreeReader` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeReader.h`) \u2014 either `MergeTreeReaderWide` or `MergeTreeReaderCompact`\n\n`MergeTreeReadPool` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.h`) distributes mark ranges across parallel reader threads for multi-threaded scanning.\n\n---\n\n## Key Source Files Reference\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h` | Base class for all MergeTree variants; manages the active parts set, metadata, and shared state |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h` | Abstract data part interface; defines part structure, metadata, and state transitions |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp` | Write path: splits blocks by partition, sorts, and writes temp parts |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp` | Pipeline sink for INSERT; coordinates writing and committing temp parts |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.h` | Low-level part writer: produces `.bin`, `.mrk2`, `primary.idx`, skip index files |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp` | Merge selection logic: chooses which parts to merge and executes merges |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.h` | Coroutine-based merge executor with horizontal, vertical, and projection stages |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp` | Merge task implementation |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp` | Read path: partition pruning, primary index scan, skip index filtering, read plan |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.h` | Translates WHERE expressions into primary key range conditions for index scan |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp` | Reads mark ranges from parts with PREWHERE support |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.h` | Distributes mark ranges across parallel reader threads |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularity.h` | Index granularity abstraction (constant vs. adaptive granule sizes) |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartState.h` | Part lifecycle state machine (Temporary \u2192 PreActive \u2192 Active \u2192 Outdated \u2192 Deleting) |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWide.h` | Wide format: one file per column (used for larger parts) |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartCompact.h` | Compact format: all columns in one file (used for small/fresh parts) |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.h` | Partition-level pruning using the partition key expression |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeBackgroundExecutor.h` | Thread pool executor for background merge/mutation tasks |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/SimpleMergeSelector.h` | Default merge selector: balances size, count, and age heuristics |\n\n---\n\n## MergeTree Engine Variants\n\nAll engine variants share the same storage architecture but differ in their merge behavior:\n\n| Engine | Merge behavior | Controlled by |\n|--------|---------------|---------------|\n| `MergeTree` | Ordinary: no deduplication, just sorting | \u2014 |\n| `ReplacingMergeTree` | Keep only the latest version per primary key | `version_column`, `is_deleted_column` |\n| `SummingMergeTree` | Sum numeric columns per primary key | `columns_to_sum` |\n| `AggregatingMergeTree` | Merge aggregate function states per key | aggregate function column types |\n| `CollapsingMergeTree` | Cancel pairs of rows via sign column | `sign_column` |\n| `VersionedCollapsingMergeTree` | Collapsing with explicit version | `sign_column`, `version_column` |\n| `GraphiteMergeTree` | Rollup time-series data | `graphite_rollup_params` |\n\nThe merge algorithm for each variant is implemented in `src/Processors/Merges/Algorithms/` and selected in `MergeTreeDataWriter::mergeBlock()` and `MergeTask`.\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Data Flow\n\n```\nINSERT\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\nsplitBlockIntoParts() # ClickHouse MergeTree Storage Engine: Architecture Analysis

## Overview

MergeTree is ClickHouse's primary table engine family, designed for high-throughput ingestion and efficient analytical queries. The core idea is **incremental sorted storage**: INSERTs produce small sorted parts, which background merges combine into larger sorted parts. Queries skip irrelevant data using multi-level indexing.

---

## High-Level Architecture Diagram

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                         MergeTree Table                             │
│                                                                     │
│  ┌──────────────┐  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │   INSERT     │  │            Data Parts (on disk)          │    │
│  │   path       │  │                                          │    │
│  │              │  │  partition_id_min_max_level/             │    │
│  │ MergeTreeSink│  │  ├── primary.idx   (primary key index)  │    │
│  │     │        │  │  ├── [col].bin     (column data)        │    │
│  │     ▼        │  │  ├── [col].mrk2   (mark files)         │    │
│  │ MergeTree    │  │  ├── skp_idx_*.idx (skip indices)       │    │
│  │ DataWriter   │  │  ├── checksums.txt                      │    │
│  │     │        │  │  ├── columns.txt                        │    │
│  │     ▼        │  │  ├── count.txt                          │    │
│  │ MergedBlock  │  │  ├── partition.dat                      │    │
│  │ OutputStream │  │  └── minmax_[col].idx                   │    │
│  └──────┬───────┘  └──────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│         │                         ▲                   ▲            │
│         │ write temp part         │ merge             │ read        │
│

# ClickHouse MergeTree Storage Engine: Architecture Analysis

## Overview

MergeTree is ClickHouse's primary table engine family, designed for high-throughput ingestion and efficient analytical queries. The core idea is **incremental sorted storage**: INSERTs produce small sorted parts, which background merges combine into larger sorted parts. Queries skip irrelevant data using multi-level indexing.

---
```
